00131 /* VARARGS */
00132 void
00133 bpf_error(const char *fmt, ...)
00134 {
00135     va_list ap;
00136 
00137     va_start(ap, fmt);
00138     if (bpf_pcap != NULL)
00139         (void)vsnprintf(pcap_geterr(bpf_pcap), PCAP_ERRBUF_SIZE,
00140             fmt, ap);
00141     va_end(ap);
00142     longjmp(top_ctx, 1);
00143     /* NOTREACHED */
00144 }

00154 /*
00155  * Value passed to gen_load_a() to indicate what the offset argument
00156  * is relative to.
00157  */
00158 enum e_offrel {
00159     OR_PACKET,  /* relative to the beginning of the packet */
00160     OR_LINK,    /* relative to the beginning of the link-layer header */
00161     OR_MACPL,   /* relative to the end of the MAC-layer header */
00162     OR_NET,     /* relative to the network-layer header */
00163     OR_NET_NOSNAP,  /* relative to the network-layer header, with no SNAP header at the link layer */
00164     OR_TRAN_IPV4,   /* relative to the transport-layer header, with IPv4 network layer */
00165     OR_TRAN_IPV6    /* relative to the transport-layer header, with IPv6 network layer */
00166 };

00169 /*
00170  * As errors are handled by a longjmp, anything allocated must be freed
00171  * in the longjmp handler, so it must be reachable from that handler.
00172  * One thing that's allocated is the result of pcap_nametoaddrinfo();
00173  * it must be freed with freeaddrinfo().  This variable points to any
00174  * addrinfo structure that would need to be freed.
00175  */
00176 static struct addrinfo *ai;

00179 /*
00180  * We divy out chunks of memory rather than call malloc each time so
00181  * we don't have to worry about leaking memory.  It's probably
00182  * not a big deal if all this memory was wasted but if this ever
00183  * goes into a library that would probably not be a good idea.
00184  *
00185  * XXX - this *is* in a library....
00186  */
00187 #define NCHUNKS 16
00188 #define CHUNK0SIZE 1024
00189 struct chunk {
00190     u_int n_left;
00191     void *m;
00192 };
00193

00285 static void *
00286 newchunk(n)
00287     u_int n;
00288 {
00289     struct chunk *cp;
00290     int k;
00291     size_t size;
00292 
00293 #ifndef __NetBSD__
00294     /* XXX Round up to nearest long. */
00295     n = (n + sizeof(long) - 1) & ~(sizeof(long) - 1);
00296 #else
00297     /* XXX Round up to structure boundary. */
00298     n = ALIGN(n);
00299 #endif
00300 
00301     cp = &chunks[cur_chunk];
00302     if (n > cp->n_left) {
00303         ++cp, k = ++cur_chunk;
00304         if (k >= NCHUNKS)
00305             bpf_error("out of memory");
00306         size = CHUNK0SIZE << k;
00307         cp->m = (void *)malloc(size);
00308         if (cp->m == NULL)
00309             bpf_error("out of memory");
00310         memset((char *)cp->m, 0, size);
00311         cp->n_left = size;
00312         if (n > size)
00313             bpf_error("out of memory");
00314     }
00315     cp->n_left -= n;
00316     return (void *)((char *)cp->m + cp->n_left);
00317 }
00318 
00319 static void
00320 freechunks()
00321 {
00322     int i;
00323 
00324     cur_chunk = 0;
00325     for (i = 0; i < NCHUNKS; ++i)
00326         if (chunks[i].m != NULL) {
00327             free(chunks[i].m);
00328             chunks[i].m = NULL;
00329         }
00330 }
00331 
00332 /*
00333  * A strdup whose allocations are freed after code generation is over.
00334  */
00335 char *
00336 sdup(s)
00337     register const char *s;
00338 {
00339     int n = strlen(s) + 1;
00340     char *cp = newchunk(n);
00341 
00342     strlcpy(cp, s, n);
00343     return (cp);
00344 }

00346 static inline struct block *
00347 new_block(code)
00348     int code;
00349 {
00350     struct block *p;
00351 
00352     p = (struct block *)newchunk(sizeof(*p));
00353     p->s.code = code;
00354     p->head = p;
00355 
00356     return p;
00357 }

00371 static struct block *
00372 gen_retblk(v)
00373     int v;
00374 {
00375     struct block *b = new_block(BPF_RET|BPF_K);
00376 
00377     b->s.k = v;
00378     return b;

00387 static bpf_u_int32 netmask;
00388 static int snaplen;
00389 int no_optimize;
00390 #ifdef WIN32
00391 static int
00392 pcap_compile_unsafe(pcap_t *p, struct bpf_program *program,
00393          const char *buf, int optimize, bpf_u_int32 mask);
00394 
00395 int
00396 pcap_compile(pcap_t *p, struct bpf_program *program,
00397          const char *buf, int optimize, bpf_u_int32 mask)
00398 {
00399     int result;
00400 
00401     EnterCriticalSection(&g_PcapCompileCriticalSection);
00402 
00403     result = pcap_compile_unsafe(p, program, buf, optimize, mask);
00404 
00405     LeaveCriticalSection(&g_PcapCompileCriticalSection);
00406     
00407     return result;
00408 }
00409 
00410 static int
00411 pcap_compile_unsafe(pcap_t *p, struct bpf_program *program,
00412          const char *buf, int optimize, bpf_u_int32 mask)
00413 #else /* WIN32 */
00414 int
00415 pcap_compile(pcap_t *p, struct bpf_program *program,
00416          const char *buf, int optimize, bpf_u_int32 mask)
00417 #endif /* WIN32 */
00418 {
00419     extern int n_errors;
00420     const char * volatile xbuf = buf;
00421     int len;
00422 
00423     no_optimize = 0;
00424     n_errors = 0;
00425     root = NULL;
00426     bpf_pcap = p;
00427     init_regs();
00428     if (setjmp(top_ctx)) {
00429 #ifdef INET6
00430         if (ai != NULL) {
00431             freeaddrinfo(ai);
00432             ai = NULL;
00433         }
00434 #endif
00435         lex_cleanup();
00436         freechunks();
00437         return (-1);
00438     }
00439 
00440     netmask = mask;
00441 
00442     snaplen = pcap_snapshot(p);
00443     if (snaplen == 0) {
00444         snprintf(p->errbuf, PCAP_ERRBUF_SIZE,
00445              "snaplen of 0 rejects all packets");
00446         return -1;
00447     }
00448 
00449     lex_init(xbuf ? xbuf : "");
00450     init_linktype(p);
00451     (void)pcap_parse();
00452 
00453     if (n_errors)
00454         syntax();
00455 
00456     if (root == NULL)
00457         root = gen_retblk(snaplen);
00458 
00459     if (optimize && !no_optimize) {
00460         bpf_optimize(&root);
00461         if (root == NULL ||
00462             (root->s.code == (BPF_RET|BPF_K) && root->s.k == 0))
00463             bpf_error("expression rejects all packets");
00464     }
00465     program->bf_insns = icode_to_fcode(root, &len);
00466     program->bf_len = len;
00467 
00468     lex_cleanup();
00469     freechunks();
00470     return (0);
00471 }
00472 
00473 /*
00474  * entry point for using the compiler with no pcap open
00475  * pass in all the stuff that is needed explicitly instead.
00476  */
00477 int
00478 pcap_compile_nopcap(int snaplen_arg, int linktype_arg,
00479             struct bpf_program *program,
00480          const char *buf, int optimize, bpf_u_int32 mask)
00481 {
00482     pcap_t *p;
00483     int ret;
00484 
00485     p = pcap_open_dead(linktype_arg, snaplen_arg);
00486     if (p == NULL)
00487         return (-1);
00488     ret = pcap_compile(p, program, buf, optimize, mask);
00489     pcap_close(p);
00490     return (ret);
00491 }

00493 /*
00494  * Clean up a "struct bpf_program" by freeing all the memory allocated
00495  * in it.
00496  */
00497 void
00498 pcap_freecode(struct bpf_program *program)
00499 {
00500     program->bf_len = 0;
00501     if (program->bf_insns != NULL) {
00502         free((char *)program->bf_insns);
00503         program->bf_insns = NULL;
00504     }
00505 }
00506 
00507 /*
00508  * Backpatch the blocks in 'list' to 'target'.  The 'sense' field indicates
00509  * which of the jt and jf fields has been resolved and which is a pointer
00510  * back to another unresolved block (or nil).  At least one of the fields
00511  * in each block is already resolved.
00512  */
00513 static void
00514 backpatch(list, target)
00515     struct block *list, *target;
00516 {
00517     struct block *next;
00518 
00519     while (list) {
00520         if (!list->sense) {
00521             next = JT(list);
00522             JT(list) = target;
00523         } else {
00524             next = JF(list);
00525             JF(list) = target;
00526         }
00527         list = next;
00528     }
00529 }
00530 
00531 /*
00532  * Merge the lists in b0 and b1, using the 'sense' field to indicate
00533  * which of jt and jf is the link.
00534  */
00535 static void
00536 merge(b0, b1)
00537     struct block *b0, *b1;
00538 {
00539     register struct block **p = &b0;
00540 
00541     /* Find end of list. */
00542     while (*p)
00543         p = !((*p)->sense) ? &JT(*p) : &JF(*p);
00544 
00545     /* Concatenate the lists. */
00546     *p = b1;
00547 }
00548 
00549 void
00550 finish_parse(p)
00551     struct block *p;
00552 {
00553     struct block *ppi_dlt_check;
00554 
00555     /*
00556      * Insert before the statements of the first (root) block any
00557      * statements needed to load the lengths of any variable-length
00558      * headers into registers.
00559      *
00560      * XXX - a fancier strategy would be to insert those before the
00561      * statements of all blocks that use those lengths and that
00562      * have no predecessors that use them, so that we only compute
00563      * the lengths if we need them.  There might be even better
00564      * approaches than that.
00565      *
00566      * However, those strategies would be more complicated, and
00567      * as we don't generate code to compute a length if the
00568      * program has no tests that use the length, and as most
00569      * tests will probably use those lengths, we would just
00570      * postpone computing the lengths so that it's not done
00571      * for tests that fail early, and it's not clear that's
00572      * worth the effort.
00573      */
00574     insert_compute_vloffsets(p->head);
00575     
00576     /*
00577      * For DLT_PPI captures, generate a check of the per-packet
00578      * DLT value to make sure it's DLT_IEEE802_11.
00579      */
00580     ppi_dlt_check = gen_ppi_dlt_check();
00581     if (ppi_dlt_check != NULL)
00582         gen_and(ppi_dlt_check, p);
00583 
00584     backpatch(p, gen_retblk(snaplen));
00585     p->sense = !p->sense;
00586     backpatch(p, gen_retblk(0));
00587     root = p->head;
00588 }
00589 
00590 void
00591 gen_and(b0, b1)
00592     struct block *b0, *b1;
00593 {
00594     backpatch(b0, b1->head);
00595     b0->sense = !b0->sense;
00596     b1->sense = !b1->sense;
00597     merge(b1, b0);
00598     b1->sense = !b1->sense;
00599     b1->head = b0->head;
00600 }
00601 
00602 void
00603 gen_or(b0, b1)
00604     struct block *b0, *b1;
00605 {
00606     b0->sense = !b0->sense;
00607     backpatch(b0, b1->head);
00608     b0->sense = !b0->sense;
00609     merge(b1, b0);
00610     b1->head = b0->head;
00611 }
00612 
00613 void
00614 gen_not(b)
00615     struct block *b;
00616 {
00617     b->sense = !b->sense;
00618 }

00647 static struct block *
00648 gen_cmp_lt(offrel, offset, size, v)
00649     enum e_offrel offrel;
00650     u_int offset, size;
00651     bpf_int32 v;
00652 {
00653     return gen_ncmp(offrel, offset, size, 0xffffffff, BPF_JGE, 1, v);
00654 }
00655 
00656 static struct block *
00657 gen_cmp_le(offrel, offset, size, v)
00658     enum e_offrel offrel;
00659     u_int offset, size;
00660     bpf_int32 v;
00661 {
00662     return gen_ncmp(offrel, offset, size, 0xffffffff, BPF_JGT, 1, v);
00663 }
00664 
00665 static struct block *
00666 gen_mcmp(offrel, offset, size, v, mask)
00667     enum e_offrel offrel;
00668     u_int offset, size;
00669     bpf_int32 v;
00670     bpf_u_int32 mask;
00671 {
00672     return gen_ncmp(offrel, offset, size, mask, BPF_JEQ, 0, v);
00673 }
00674 
00675 static struct block *
00676 gen_bcmp(offrel, offset, size, v)
00677     enum e_offrel offrel;
00678     register u_int offset, size;
00679     register const u_char *v;
00680 {
00681     register struct block *b, *tmp;
00682 
00683     b = NULL;
00684     while (size >= 4) {
00685         register const u_char *p = &v[size - 4];
00686         bpf_int32 w = ((bpf_int32)p[0] << 24) |
00687             ((bpf_int32)p[1] << 16) | ((bpf_int32)p[2] << 8) | p[3];
00688 
00689         tmp = gen_cmp(offrel, offset + size - 4, BPF_W, w);
00690         if (b != NULL)
00691             gen_and(b, tmp);
00692         b = tmp;
00693         size -= 4;
00694     }
00695     while (size >= 2) {
00696         register const u_char *p = &v[size - 2];
00697         bpf_int32 w = ((bpf_int32)p[0] << 8) | p[1];
00698 
00699         tmp = gen_cmp(offrel, offset + size - 2, BPF_H, w);
00700         if (b != NULL)
00701             gen_and(b, tmp);
00702         b = tmp;
00703         size -= 2;
00704     }
00705     if (size > 0) {
00706         tmp = gen_cmp(offrel, offset, BPF_B, (bpf_int32)v[0]);
00707         if (b != NULL)
00708             gen_and(b, tmp);
00709         b = tmp;
00710     }
00711     return b;
00712 }
00713 
00714 /*
00715  * AND the field of size "size" at offset "offset" relative to the header
00716  * specified by "offrel" with "mask", and compare it with the value "v"
00717  * with the test specified by "jtype"; if "reverse" is true, the test
00718  * should test the opposite of "jtype".
00719  */
00720 static struct block *
00721 gen_ncmp(offrel, offset, size, mask, jtype, reverse, v)
00722     enum e_offrel offrel;
00723     bpf_int32 v;
00724     bpf_u_int32 offset, size, mask, jtype;
00725     int reverse;
00726 {
00727     struct slist *s, *s2;
00728     struct block *b;
00729 
00730     s = gen_load_a(offrel, offset, size);
00731 
00732     if (mask != 0xffffffff) {
00733         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_AND|BPF_K);
00734         s2->s.k = mask;
00735         sappend(s, s2);
00736     }
00737 
00738     b = new_block(JMP(jtype));
00739     b->stmts = s;
00740     b->s.k = v;
00741     if (reverse && (jtype == BPF_JGT || jtype == BPF_JGE))
00742         gen_not(b);
00743     return b;
00744 }
00745 
00746 /*
00747  * Various code constructs need to know the layout of the data link
00748  * layer.  These variables give the necessary offsets from the beginning
00749  * of the packet data.
00750  */
00751 
00752 /*
00753  * This is the offset of the beginning of the link-layer header from
00754  * the beginning of the raw packet data.
00755  *
00756  * It's usually 0, except for 802.11 with a fixed-length radio header.
00757  * (For 802.11 with a variable-length radio header, we have to generate
00758  * code to compute that offset; off_ll is 0 in that case.)
00759  */
00760 static u_int off_ll;
00761 
00762 /*
00763  * If there's a variable-length header preceding the link-layer header,
00764  * "reg_off_ll" is the register number for a register containing the
00765  * length of that header, and therefore the offset of the link-layer
00766  * header from the beginning of the raw packet data.  Otherwise,
00767  * "reg_off_ll" is -1.
00768  */
00769 static int reg_off_ll;
00770 
00771 /*
00772  * This is the offset of the beginning of the MAC-layer header from
00773  * the beginning of the link-layer header.
00774  * It's usually 0, except for ATM LANE, where it's the offset, relative
00775  * to the beginning of the raw packet data, of the Ethernet header.
00776  */
00777 static u_int off_mac;
00778 
00779 /*
00780  * This is the offset of the beginning of the MAC-layer payload,
00781  * from the beginning of the raw packet data.
00782  *
00783  * I.e., it's the sum of the length of the link-layer header (without,
00784  * for example, any 802.2 LLC header, so it's the MAC-layer
00785  * portion of that header), plus any prefix preceding the
00786  * link-layer header.
00787  */
00788 static u_int off_macpl;
00789 
00790 /*
00791  * This is 1 if the offset of the beginning of the MAC-layer payload
00792  * from the beginning of the link-layer header is variable-length.
00793  */
00794 static int off_macpl_is_variable;
00795 
00796 /*
00797  * If the link layer has variable_length headers, "reg_off_macpl"
00798  * is the register number for a register containing the length of the
00799  * link-layer header plus the length of any variable-length header
00800  * preceding the link-layer header.  Otherwise, "reg_off_macpl"
00801  * is -1.
00802  */
00803 static int reg_off_macpl;
00804 
00805 /*
00806  * "off_linktype" is the offset to information in the link-layer header
00807  * giving the packet type.  This offset is relative to the beginning
00808  * of the link-layer header (i.e., it doesn't include off_ll).
00809  *
00810  * For Ethernet, it's the offset of the Ethernet type field.
00811  *
00812  * For link-layer types that always use 802.2 headers, it's the
00813  * offset of the LLC header.
00814  *
00815  * For PPP, it's the offset of the PPP type field.
00816  *
00817  * For Cisco HDLC, it's the offset of the CHDLC type field.
00818  *
00819  * For BSD loopback, it's the offset of the AF_ value.
00820  *
00821  * For Linux cooked sockets, it's the offset of the type field.
00822  *
00823  * It's set to -1 for no encapsulation, in which case, IP is assumed.
00824  */
00825 static u_int off_linktype;
00826 
00827 /*
00828  * TRUE if "pppoes" appeared in the filter; it causes link-layer type
00829  * checks to check the PPP header, assumed to follow a LAN-style link-
00830  * layer header and a PPPoE session header.
00831  */
00832 static int is_pppoes = 0;
00833 
00834 /*
00835  * TRUE if the link layer includes an ATM pseudo-header.
00836  */
00837 static int is_atm = 0;
00838 
00839 /*
00840  * TRUE if "lane" appeared in the filter; it causes us to generate
00841  * code that assumes LANE rather than LLC-encapsulated traffic in SunATM.
00842  */
00843 static int is_lane = 0;
00844 
00845 /*
00846  * These are offsets for the ATM pseudo-header.
00847  */
00848 static u_int off_vpi;
00849 static u_int off_vci;
00850 static u_int off_proto;
00851 
00852 /*
00853  * These are offsets for the MTP2 fields.
00854  */
00855 static u_int off_li;
00856 
00857 /*
00858  * These are offsets for the MTP3 fields.
00859  */
00860 static u_int off_sio;
00861 static u_int off_opc;
00862 static u_int off_dpc;
00863 static u_int off_sls;
00864 
00865 /*
00866  * This is the offset of the first byte after the ATM pseudo_header,
00867  * or -1 if there is no ATM pseudo-header.
00868  */
00869 static u_int off_payload;
00870 
00871 /*
00872  * These are offsets to the beginning of the network-layer header.
00873  * They are relative to the beginning of the MAC-layer payload (i.e.,
00874  * they don't include off_ll or off_macpl).
00875  *
00876  * If the link layer never uses 802.2 LLC:
00877  *
00878  *  "off_nl" and "off_nl_nosnap" are the same.
00879  *
00880  * If the link layer always uses 802.2 LLC:
00881  *
00882  *  "off_nl" is the offset if there's a SNAP header following
00883  *  the 802.2 header;
00884  *
00885  *  "off_nl_nosnap" is the offset if there's no SNAP header.
00886  *
00887  * If the link layer is Ethernet:
00888  *
00889  *  "off_nl" is the offset if the packet is an Ethernet II packet
00890  *  (we assume no 802.3+802.2+SNAP);
00891  *
00892  *  "off_nl_nosnap" is the offset if the packet is an 802.3 packet
00893  *  with an 802.2 header following it.
00894  */
00895 static u_int off_nl;
00896 static u_int off_nl_nosnap;
00897 
00898 static int linktype;
00899 
00900 static void
00901 init_linktype(p)
00902     pcap_t *p;
00903 {
00904     linktype = pcap_datalink(p);
00905 #ifdef PCAP_FDDIPAD
00906     pcap_fddipad = p->fddipad;
00907 #endif
00908 
00909     /*
00910      * Assume it's not raw ATM with a pseudo-header, for now.
00911      */
00912     off_mac = 0;
00913     is_atm = 0;
00914     is_lane = 0;
00915     off_vpi = -1;
00916     off_vci = -1;
00917     off_proto = -1;
00918     off_payload = -1;
00919 
00920     /*
00921      * And that we're not doing PPPoE.
00922      */
00923     is_pppoes = 0;
00924 
00925     /*
00926      * And assume we're not doing SS7.
00927      */
00928     off_li = -1;
00929     off_sio = -1;
00930     off_opc = -1;
00931     off_dpc = -1;
00932     off_sls = -1;
00933 
00934     /*
00935      * Also assume it's not 802.11.
00936      */
00937     off_ll = 0;
00938     off_macpl = 0;
00939     off_macpl_is_variable = 0;
00940 
00941     orig_linktype = -1;
00942     orig_nl = -1;
00943         label_stack_depth = 0;
00944 
00945     reg_off_ll = -1;
00946     reg_off_macpl = -1;
00947 
00948     switch (linktype) {
00949 
00950     case DLT_ARCNET:
00951         off_linktype = 2;
00952         off_macpl = 6;
00953         off_nl = 0;     /* XXX in reality, variable! */
00954         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
00955         return;
00956 
00957     case DLT_ARCNET_LINUX:
00958         off_linktype = 4;
00959         off_macpl = 8;
00960         off_nl = 0;     /* XXX in reality, variable! */
00961         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
00962         return;
00963 
00964     case DLT_EN10MB:
00965         off_linktype = 12;
00966         off_macpl = 14;     /* Ethernet header length */
00967         off_nl = 0;     /* Ethernet II */
00968         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.3+802.2 */
00969         return;
00970 
00971     case DLT_SLIP:
00972         /*
00973          * SLIP doesn't have a link level type.  The 16 byte
00974          * header is hacked into our SLIP driver.
00975          */
00976         off_linktype = -1;
00977         off_macpl = 16;
00978         off_nl = 0;
00979         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
00980         return;
00981 
00982     case DLT_SLIP_BSDOS:
00983         /* XXX this may be the same as the DLT_PPP_BSDOS case */
00984         off_linktype = -1;
00985         /* XXX end */
00986         off_macpl = 24;
00987         off_nl = 0;
00988         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
00989         return;
00990 
00991     case DLT_NULL:
00992     case DLT_LOOP:
00993         off_linktype = 0;
00994         off_macpl = 4;
00995         off_nl = 0;
00996         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
00997         return;
00998 
00999     case DLT_ENC:
01000         off_linktype = 0;
01001         off_macpl = 12;
01002         off_nl = 0;
01003         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01004         return;
01005 
01006     case DLT_PPP:
01007     case DLT_PPP_PPPD:
01008     case DLT_C_HDLC:        /* BSD/OS Cisco HDLC */
01009     case DLT_PPP_SERIAL:        /* NetBSD sync/async serial PPP */
01010         off_linktype = 2;
01011         off_macpl = 4;
01012         off_nl = 0;
01013         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01014         return;
01015 
01016     case DLT_PPP_ETHER:
01017         /*
01018          * This does no include the Ethernet header, and
01019          * only covers session state.
01020          */
01021         off_linktype = 6;
01022         off_macpl = 8;
01023         off_nl = 0;
01024         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01025         return;
01026 
01027     case DLT_PPP_BSDOS:
01028         off_linktype = 5;
01029         off_macpl = 24;
01030         off_nl = 0;
01031         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01032         return;
01033 
01034     case DLT_FDDI:
01035         /*
01036          * FDDI doesn't really have a link-level type field.
01037          * We set "off_linktype" to the offset of the LLC header.
01038          *
01039          * To check for Ethernet types, we assume that SSAP = SNAP
01040          * is being used and pick out the encapsulated Ethernet type.
01041          * XXX - should we generate code to check for SNAP?
01042          */
01043         off_linktype = 13;
01044 #ifdef PCAP_FDDIPAD
01045         off_linktype += pcap_fddipad;
01046 #endif
01047         off_macpl = 13;     /* FDDI MAC header length */
01048 #ifdef PCAP_FDDIPAD
01049         off_macpl += pcap_fddipad;
01050 #endif
01051         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01052         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01053         return;
01054 
01055     case DLT_IEEE802:
01056         /*
01057          * Token Ring doesn't really have a link-level type field.
01058          * We set "off_linktype" to the offset of the LLC header.
01059          *
01060          * To check for Ethernet types, we assume that SSAP = SNAP
01061          * is being used and pick out the encapsulated Ethernet type.
01062          * XXX - should we generate code to check for SNAP?
01063          *
01064          * XXX - the header is actually variable-length.
01065          * Some various Linux patched versions gave 38
01066          * as "off_linktype" and 40 as "off_nl"; however,
01067          * if a token ring packet has *no* routing
01068          * information, i.e. is not source-routed, the correct
01069          * values are 20 and 22, as they are in the vanilla code.
01070          *
01071          * A packet is source-routed iff the uppermost bit
01072          * of the first byte of the source address, at an
01073          * offset of 8, has the uppermost bit set.  If the
01074          * packet is source-routed, the total number of bytes
01075          * of routing information is 2 plus bits 0x1F00 of
01076          * the 16-bit value at an offset of 14 (shifted right
01077          * 8 - figure out which byte that is).
01078          */
01079         off_linktype = 14;
01080         off_macpl = 14;     /* Token Ring MAC header length */
01081         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01082         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01083         return;
01084 
01085     case DLT_IEEE802_11:
01086     case DLT_PRISM_HEADER:
01087     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO_AVS:
01088     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO:
01089         /*
01090          * 802.11 doesn't really have a link-level type field.
01091          * We set "off_linktype" to the offset of the LLC header.
01092          *
01093          * To check for Ethernet types, we assume that SSAP = SNAP
01094          * is being used and pick out the encapsulated Ethernet type.
01095          * XXX - should we generate code to check for SNAP?
01096          *
01097          * We also handle variable-length radio headers here.
01098          * The Prism header is in theory variable-length, but in
01099          * practice it's always 144 bytes long.  However, some
01100          * drivers on Linux use ARPHRD_IEEE80211_PRISM, but
01101          * sometimes or always supply an AVS header, so we
01102          * have to check whether the radio header is a Prism
01103          * header or an AVS header, so, in practice, it's
01104          * variable-length.
01105          */
01106         off_linktype = 24;
01107         off_macpl = 0;      /* link-layer header is variable-length */
01108         off_macpl_is_variable = 1;
01109         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01110         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01111         return;
01112 
01113     case DLT_PPI:
01114         /* 
01115          * At the moment we treat PPI the same way that we treat
01116          * normal Radiotap encoded packets. The difference is in
01117          * the function that generates the code at the beginning
01118          * to compute the header length.  Since this code generator
01119          * of PPI supports bare 802.11 encapsulation only (i.e.
01120          * the encapsulated DLT should be DLT_IEEE802_11) we
01121          * generate code to check for this too.
01122          */
01123         off_linktype = 24;
01124         off_macpl = 0;      /* link-layer header is variable-length */
01125         off_macpl_is_variable = 1;
01126         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01127         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01128         return;
01129 
01130     case DLT_ATM_RFC1483:
01131     case DLT_ATM_CLIP:  /* Linux ATM defines this */
01132         /*
01133          * assume routed, non-ISO PDUs
01134          * (i.e., LLC = 0xAA-AA-03, OUT = 0x00-00-00)
01135          *
01136          * XXX - what about ISO PDUs, e.g. CLNP, ISIS, ESIS,
01137          * or PPP with the PPP NLPID (e.g., PPPoA)?  The
01138          * latter would presumably be treated the way PPPoE
01139          * should be, so you can do "pppoe and udp port 2049"
01140          * or "pppoa and tcp port 80" and have it check for
01141          * PPPo{A,E} and a PPP protocol of IP and....
01142          */
01143         off_linktype = 0;
01144         off_macpl = 0;      /* packet begins with LLC header */
01145         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01146         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01147         return;
01148 
01149     case DLT_SUNATM:
01150         /*
01151          * Full Frontal ATM; you get AALn PDUs with an ATM
01152          * pseudo-header.
01153          */
01154         is_atm = 1;
01155         off_vpi = SUNATM_VPI_POS;
01156         off_vci = SUNATM_VCI_POS;
01157         off_proto = PROTO_POS;
01158         off_mac = -1;   /* assume LLC-encapsulated, so no MAC-layer header */
01159         off_payload = SUNATM_PKT_BEGIN_POS;
01160         off_linktype = off_payload;
01161         off_macpl = off_payload;    /* if LLC-encapsulated */
01162         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01163         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01164         return;
01165 
01166     case DLT_RAW:
01167     case DLT_IPV4:
01168     case DLT_IPV6:
01169         off_linktype = -1;
01170         off_macpl = 0;
01171         off_nl = 0;
01172         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01173         return;
01174 
01175     case DLT_LINUX_SLL: /* fake header for Linux cooked socket */
01176         off_linktype = 14;
01177         off_macpl = 16;
01178         off_nl = 0;
01179         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01180         return;
01181 
01182     case DLT_LTALK:
01183         /*
01184          * LocalTalk does have a 1-byte type field in the LLAP header,
01185          * but really it just indicates whether there is a "short" or
01186          * "long" DDP packet following.
01187          */
01188         off_linktype = -1;
01189         off_macpl = 0;
01190         off_nl = 0;
01191         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01192         return;
01193 
01194     case DLT_IP_OVER_FC:
01195         /*
01196          * RFC 2625 IP-over-Fibre-Channel doesn't really have a
01197          * link-level type field.  We set "off_linktype" to the
01198          * offset of the LLC header.
01199          *
01200          * To check for Ethernet types, we assume that SSAP = SNAP
01201          * is being used and pick out the encapsulated Ethernet type.
01202          * XXX - should we generate code to check for SNAP? RFC
01203          * 2625 says SNAP should be used.
01204          */
01205         off_linktype = 16;
01206         off_macpl = 16;
01207         off_nl = 8;     /* 802.2+SNAP */
01208         off_nl_nosnap = 3;  /* 802.2 */
01209         return;
01210 
01211     case DLT_FRELAY:
01212         /*
01213          * XXX - we should set this to handle SNAP-encapsulated
01214          * frames (NLPID of 0x80).
01215          */
01216         off_linktype = -1;
01217         off_macpl = 0;
01218         off_nl = 0;
01219         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01220         return;
01221 
01222                 /*
01223                  * the only BPF-interesting FRF.16 frames are non-control frames;
01224                  * Frame Relay has a variable length link-layer
01225                  * so lets start with offset 4 for now and increments later on (FIXME);
01226                  */
01227     case DLT_MFR:
01228         off_linktype = -1;
01229         off_macpl = 0;
01230         off_nl = 4;
01231         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* XXX - for now -> no 802.2 LLC */
01232         return;
01233 
01234     case DLT_APPLE_IP_OVER_IEEE1394:
01235         off_linktype = 16;
01236         off_macpl = 18;
01237         off_nl = 0;
01238         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01239         return;
01240 
01241     case DLT_LINUX_IRDA:
01242         /*
01243          * Currently, only raw "link[N:M]" filtering is supported.
01244          */
01245         off_linktype = -1;
01246         off_macpl = -1;
01247         off_nl = -1;
01248         off_nl_nosnap = -1;
01249         return;
01250 
01251     case DLT_DOCSIS:
01252         /*
01253          * Currently, only raw "link[N:M]" filtering is supported.
01254          */
01255         off_linktype = -1;
01256         off_macpl = -1;
01257         off_nl = -1;
01258         off_nl_nosnap = -1;
01259         return;
01260 
01261     case DLT_SYMANTEC_FIREWALL:
01262         off_linktype = 6;
01263         off_macpl = 44;
01264         off_nl = 0;     /* Ethernet II */
01265         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* XXX - what does it do with 802.3 packets? */
01266         return;
01267 
01268 #ifdef HAVE_NET_PFVAR_H
01269     case DLT_PFLOG:
01270         off_linktype = 0;
01271         off_macpl = PFLOG_HDRLEN;
01272         off_nl = 0;
01273         off_nl_nosnap = 0;  /* no 802.2 LLC */
01274         return;
01275 #endif
01276 
01277         case DLT_JUNIPER_MFR:
01278         case DLT_JUNIPER_MLFR:
01279         case DLT_JUNIPER_MLPPP:

01595 
01596 /*
01597  * Load a value relative to the beginning of the link-layer header.
01598  * The link-layer header doesn't necessarily begin at the beginning
01599  * of the packet data; there might be a variable-length prefix containing
01600  * radio information.
01601  */
01602 static struct slist *
01603 gen_load_llrel(offset, size)
01604     u_int offset, size;
01605 {
01606     struct slist *s, *s2;
01607 
01608     s = gen_llprefixlen();
01609 
01610     /*
01611      * If "s" is non-null, it has code to arrange that the X register
01612      * contains the length of the prefix preceding the link-layer
01613      * header.
01614      *
01615      * Otherwise, the length of the prefix preceding the link-layer
01616      * header is "off_ll".
01617      */
01618     if (s != NULL) {
01619         /*
01620          * There's a variable-length prefix preceding the
01621          * link-layer header.  "s" points to a list of statements
01622          * that put the length of that prefix into the X register.
01623          * do an indirect load, to use the X register as an offset.
01624          */
01625         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_IND|size);
01626         s2->s.k = offset;
01627         sappend(s, s2);
01628     } else {
01629         /*
01630          * There is no variable-length header preceding the
01631          * link-layer header; add in off_ll, which, if there's
01632          * a fixed-length header preceding the link-layer header,
01633          * is the length of that header.
01634          */
01635         s = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_ABS|size);
01636         s->s.k = offset + off_ll;
01637     }
01638     return s;
01639 }
01640 
01641 /*
01642  * Load a value relative to the beginning of the MAC-layer payload.
01643  */
01644 static struct slist *
01645 gen_load_macplrel(offset, size)
01646     u_int offset, size;
01647 {
01648     struct slist *s, *s2;
01649 
01650     s = gen_off_macpl();
01651 
01652     /*
01653      * If s is non-null, the offset of the MAC-layer payload is
01654      * variable, and s points to a list of instructions that
01655      * arrange that the X register contains that offset.
01656      *
01657      * Otherwise, the offset of the MAC-layer payload is constant,
01658      * and is in off_macpl.
01659      */
01660     if (s != NULL) {
01661         /*
01662          * The offset of the MAC-layer payload is in the X
01663          * register.  Do an indirect load, to use the X register
01664          * as an offset.
01665          */
01666         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_IND|size);
01667         s2->s.k = offset;
01668         sappend(s, s2);
01669     } else {
01670         /*
01671          * The offset of the MAC-layer payload is constant,
01672          * and is in off_macpl; load the value at that offset
01673          * plus the specified offset.
01674          */
01675         s = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_ABS|size);
01676         s->s.k = off_macpl + offset;
01677     }
01678     return s;
01679 }
01680 
01681 /*
01682  * Load a value relative to the beginning of the specified header.
01683  */
01684 static struct slist *
01685 gen_load_a(offrel, offset, size)
01686     enum e_offrel offrel;
01687     u_int offset, size;
01688 {
01689     struct slist *s, *s2;
01690 
01691     switch (offrel) {
01692 
01693     case OR_PACKET:
01694                 s = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_ABS|size);
01695                 s->s.k = offset;
01696         break;
01697 
01698     case OR_LINK:
01699         s = gen_load_llrel(offset, size);
01700         break;
01701 
01702     case OR_MACPL:
01703         s = gen_load_macplrel(offset, size);
01704         break;
01705 
01706     case OR_NET:
01707         s = gen_load_macplrel(off_nl + offset, size);
01708         break;
01709 
01710     case OR_NET_NOSNAP:
01711         s = gen_load_macplrel(off_nl_nosnap + offset, size);
01712         break;
01713 
01714     case OR_TRAN_IPV4:
01715         /*
01716          * Load the X register with the length of the IPv4 header
01717          * (plus the offset of the link-layer header, if it's
01718          * preceded by a variable-length header such as a radio
01719          * header), in bytes.
01720          */
01721         s = gen_loadx_iphdrlen();
01722 
01723         /*
01724          * Load the item at {offset of the MAC-layer payload} +
01725          * {offset, relative to the start of the MAC-layer
01726          * paylod, of the IPv4 header} + {length of the IPv4 header} +
01727          * {specified offset}.
01728          *
01729          * (If the offset of the MAC-layer payload is variable,
01730          * it's included in the value in the X register, and
01731          * off_macpl is 0.)
01732          */
01733         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_IND|size);
01734         s2->s.k = off_macpl + off_nl + offset;
01735         sappend(s, s2);
01736         break;
01737 
01738     case OR_TRAN_IPV6:
01739         s = gen_load_macplrel(off_nl + 40 + offset, size);
01740         break;
01741 
01742     default:
01743         abort();
01744         return NULL;
01745     }
01746     return s;
01747 }
01748 
01749 /*
01750  * Generate code to load into the X register the sum of the length of
01751  * the IPv4 header and any variable-length header preceding the link-layer
01752  * header.
01753  */
01754 static struct slist *
01755 gen_loadx_iphdrlen()
01756 {
01757     struct slist *s, *s2;
01758 
01759     s = gen_off_macpl();
01760     if (s != NULL) {
01761         /*
01762          * There's a variable-length prefix preceding the
01763          * link-layer header, or the link-layer header is itself
01764          * variable-length.  "s" points to a list of statements
01765          * that put the offset of the MAC-layer payload into
01766          * the X register.
01767          *
01768          * The 4*([k]&0xf) addressing mode can't be used, as we
01769          * don't have a constant offset, so we have to load the
01770          * value in question into the A register and add to it
01771          * the value from the X register.
01772          */
01773         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_IND|BPF_B);
01774         s2->s.k = off_nl;
01775         sappend(s, s2);
01776         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_AND|BPF_K);
01777         s2->s.k = 0xf;
01778         sappend(s, s2);
01779         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_LSH|BPF_K);
01780         s2->s.k = 2;
01781         sappend(s, s2);
01782 
01783         /*
01784          * The A register now contains the length of the
01785          * IP header.  We need to add to it the offset of
01786          * the MAC-layer payload, which is still in the X
01787          * register, and move the result into the X register.
01788          */
01789         sappend(s, new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_ADD|BPF_X));
01790         sappend(s, new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX));
01791     } else {
01792         /*
01793          * There is no variable-length header preceding the
01794          * link-layer header, and the link-layer header is
01795          * fixed-length; load the length of the IPv4 header,
01796          * which is at an offset of off_nl from the beginning
01797          * of the MAC-layer payload, and thus at an offset
01798          * of off_mac_pl + off_nl from the beginning of the
01799          * raw packet data.
01800          */
01801         s = new_stmt(BPF_LDX|BPF_MSH|BPF_B);
01802         s->s.k = off_macpl + off_nl;
01803     }
01804     return s;
01805 }
01806 
01807 static struct block *
01808 gen_uncond(rsense)
01809     int rsense;
01810 {
01811     struct block *b;
01812     struct slist *s;
01813 
01814     s = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_IMM);
01815     s->s.k = !rsense;
01816     b = new_block(JMP(BPF_JEQ));
01817     b->stmts = s;
01818 
01819     return b;
01820 }
01821 
01822 static inline struct block *
01823 gen_true()
01824 {
01825     return gen_uncond(1);
01826 }
01827 
01828 static inline struct block *
01829 gen_false()
01830 {
01831     return gen_uncond(0);
01832 }
01833 
01834 /*
01835  * Byte-swap a 32-bit number.
01836  * ("htonl()" or "ntohl()" won't work - we want to byte-swap even on
01837  * big-endian platforms.)
01838  */
01839 #define SWAPLONG(y) \
01840 ((((y)&0xff)<<24) | (((y)&0xff00)<<8) | (((y)&0xff0000)>>8) | (((y)>>24)&0xff))
01841 
01842 /*
01843  * Generate code to match a particular packet type.
01844  *
01845  * "proto" is an Ethernet type value, if > ETHERMTU, or an LLC SAP
01846  * value, if <= ETHERMTU.  We use that to determine whether to
01847  * match the type/length field or to check the type/length field for
01848  * a value <= ETHERMTU to see whether it's a type field and then do
01849  * the appropriate test.
01850  */
01851 static struct block *
01852 gen_ether_linktype(proto)
01853     register int proto;
01854 {
01855     struct block *b0, *b1;
01856 
01857     switch (proto) {
01858 
01859     case LLCSAP_ISONS:
01860     case LLCSAP_IP:
01861     case LLCSAP_NETBEUI:
01862         /*
01863          * OSI protocols and NetBEUI always use 802.2 encapsulation,
01864          * so we check the DSAP and SSAP.
01865          *
01866          * LLCSAP_IP checks for IP-over-802.2, rather
01867          * than IP-over-Ethernet or IP-over-SNAP.
01868          *
01869          * XXX - should we check both the DSAP and the
01870          * SSAP, like this, or should we check just the
01871          * DSAP, as we do for other types <= ETHERMTU
01872          * (i.e., other SAP values)?
01873          */
01874         b0 = gen_cmp_gt(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, ETHERMTU);
01875         gen_not(b0);
01876         b1 = gen_cmp(OR_MACPL, 0, BPF_H, (bpf_int32)
01877                  ((proto << 8) | proto));
01878         gen_and(b0, b1);
01879         return b1;
01880 
01881     case LLCSAP_IPX:
01882         /*
01883          * Check for;
01884          *
01885          *  Ethernet_II frames, which are Ethernet
01886          *  frames with a frame type of ETHERTYPE_IPX;
01887          *
01888          *  Ethernet_802.3 frames, which are 802.3
01889          *  frames (i.e., the type/length field is
01890          *  a length field, <= ETHERMTU, rather than
01891          *  a type field) with the first two bytes
01892          *  after the Ethernet/802.3 header being
01893          *  0xFFFF;
01894          *
01895          *  Ethernet_802.2 frames, which are 802.3
01896          *  frames with an 802.2 LLC header and
01897          *  with the IPX LSAP as the DSAP in the LLC
01898          *  header;
01899          *
01900          *  Ethernet_SNAP frames, which are 802.3
01901          *  frames with an LLC header and a SNAP
01902          *  header and with an OUI of 0x000000
01903          *  (encapsulated Ethernet) and a protocol
01904          *  ID of ETHERTYPE_IPX in the SNAP header.
01905          *
01906          * XXX - should we generate the same code both
01907          * for tests for LLCSAP_IPX and for ETHERTYPE_IPX?
01908          */
01909 
01910         /*
01911          * This generates code to check both for the
01912          * IPX LSAP (Ethernet_802.2) and for Ethernet_802.3.
01913          */
01914         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_MACPL, 0, BPF_B, (bpf_int32)LLCSAP_IPX);
01915         b1 = gen_cmp(OR_MACPL, 0, BPF_H, (bpf_int32)0xFFFF);
01916         gen_or(b0, b1);
01917 
01918         /*
01919          * Now we add code to check for SNAP frames with
01920          * ETHERTYPE_IPX, i.e. Ethernet_SNAP.
01921          */
01922         b0 = gen_snap(0x000000, ETHERTYPE_IPX);
01923         gen_or(b0, b1);
01924 
01925         /*
01926          * Now we generate code to check for 802.3
01927          * frames in general.
01928          */
01929         b0 = gen_cmp_gt(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, ETHERMTU);
01930         gen_not(b0);
01931 
01932         /*
01933          * Now add the check for 802.3 frames before the
01934          * check for Ethernet_802.2 and Ethernet_802.3,
01935          * as those checks should only be done on 802.3
01936          * frames, not on Ethernet frames.
01937          */
01938         gen_and(b0, b1);
01939 
01940         /*
01941          * Now add the check for Ethernet_II frames, and
01942          * do that before checking for the other frame
01943          * types.
01944          */
01945         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H,
01946             (bpf_int32)ETHERTYPE_IPX);
01947         gen_or(b0, b1);
01948         return b1;
01949 
01950     case ETHERTYPE_ATALK:
01951     case ETHERTYPE_AARP:
01952         /*
01953          * EtherTalk (AppleTalk protocols on Ethernet link
01954          * layer) may use 802.2 encapsulation.
01955          */
01956 
01957         /*
01958          * Check for 802.2 encapsulation (EtherTalk phase 2?);
01959          * we check for an Ethernet type field less than
01960          * 1500, which means it's an 802.3 length field.
01961          */
01962         b0 = gen_cmp_gt(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, ETHERMTU);
01963         gen_not(b0);
01964 
01965         /*
01966          * 802.2-encapsulated ETHERTYPE_ATALK packets are
01967          * SNAP packets with an organization code of
01968          * 0x080007 (Apple, for Appletalk) and a protocol
01969          * type of ETHERTYPE_ATALK (Appletalk).
01970          *
01971          * 802.2-encapsulated ETHERTYPE_AARP packets are
01972          * SNAP packets with an organization code of
01973          * 0x000000 (encapsulated Ethernet) and a protocol
01974          * type of ETHERTYPE_AARP (Appletalk ARP).
01975          */
01976         if (proto == ETHERTYPE_ATALK)
01977             b1 = gen_snap(0x080007, ETHERTYPE_ATALK);
01978         else    /* proto == ETHERTYPE_AARP */
01979             b1 = gen_snap(0x000000, ETHERTYPE_AARP);
01980         gen_and(b0, b1);
01981 
01982         /*
01983          * Check for Ethernet encapsulation (Ethertalk
01984          * phase 1?); we just check for the Ethernet
01985          * protocol type.
01986          */
01987         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, (bpf_int32)proto);
01988 
01989         gen_or(b0, b1);
01990         return b1;
01991 
01992     default:
01993         if (proto <= ETHERMTU) {
01994             /*
01995              * This is an LLC SAP value, so the frames
01996              * that match would be 802.2 frames.
01997              * Check that the frame is an 802.2 frame
01998              * (i.e., that the length/type field is
01999              * a length field, <= ETHERMTU) and
02000              * then check the DSAP.
02001              */
02002             b0 = gen_cmp_gt(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, ETHERMTU);
02003             gen_not(b0);
02004             b1 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype + 2, BPF_B,
02005                 (bpf_int32)proto);
02006             gen_and(b0, b1);
02007             return b1;
02008         } else {
02009             /*
02010              * This is an Ethernet type, so compare
02011              * the length/type field with it (if
02012              * the frame is an 802.2 frame, the length
02013              * field will be <= ETHERMTU, and, as
02014              * "proto" is > ETHERMTU, this test
02015              * will fail and the frame won't match,
02016              * which is what we want).
02017              */
02018             return gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H,
02019                 (bpf_int32)proto);
02020         }
02021     }
02022 }
02023 
02024 /*
02025  * "proto" is an Ethernet type value and for IPNET, if it is not IPv4
02026  * or IPv6 then we have an error.
02027  */
02028 static struct block *
02029 gen_ipnet_linktype(proto)
02030     register int proto;
02031 {
02032     switch (proto) {
02033 
02034     case ETHERTYPE_IP:
02035         return gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_B,
02036             (bpf_int32)IPH_AF_INET);
02037         /* NOTREACHED */
02038 
02039     case ETHERTYPE_IPV6:
02040         return gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_B,
02041             (bpf_int32)IPH_AF_INET6);
02042         /* NOTREACHED */
02043 
02044     default:
02045         break;
02046     }
02047 
02048     return gen_false();
02049 }
02050 
02051 /*
02052  * Generate code to match a particular packet type.
02053  *
02054  * "proto" is an Ethernet type value, if > ETHERMTU, or an LLC SAP
02055  * value, if <= ETHERMTU.  We use that to determine whether to
02056  * match the type field or to check the type field for the special
02057  * LINUX_SLL_P_802_2 value and then do the appropriate test.
02058  */
02059 static struct block *
02060 gen_linux_sll_linktype(proto)
02061     register int proto;
02062 {
02063     struct block *b0, *b1;
02064 
02065     switch (proto) {
02066 
02067     case LLCSAP_ISONS:
02068     case LLCSAP_IP:
02069     case LLCSAP_NETBEUI:
02070         /*
02071          * OSI protocols and NetBEUI always use 802.2 encapsulation,
02072          * so we check the DSAP and SSAP.
02073          *
02074          * LLCSAP_IP checks for IP-over-802.2, rather
02075          * than IP-over-Ethernet or IP-over-SNAP.
02076          *
02077          * XXX - should we check both the DSAP and the
02078          * SSAP, like this, or should we check just the
02079          * DSAP, as we do for other types <= ETHERMTU
02080          * (i.e., other SAP values)?
02081          */
02082         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, LINUX_SLL_P_802_2);
02083         b1 = gen_cmp(OR_MACPL, 0, BPF_H, (bpf_int32)
02084                  ((proto << 8) | proto));
02085         gen_and(b0, b1);
02086         return b1;
02087 
02088     case LLCSAP_IPX:
02089         /*
02090          *  Ethernet_II frames, which are Ethernet
02091          *  frames with a frame type of ETHERTYPE_IPX;
02092          *
02093          *  Ethernet_802.3 frames, which have a frame
02094          *  type of LINUX_SLL_P_802_3;
02095          *
02096          *  Ethernet_802.2 frames, which are 802.3
02097          *  frames with an 802.2 LLC header (i.e, have
02098          *  a frame type of LINUX_SLL_P_802_2) and
02099          *  with the IPX LSAP as the DSAP in the LLC
02100          *  header;
02101          *
02102          *  Ethernet_SNAP frames, which are 802.3
02103          *  frames with an LLC header and a SNAP
02104          *  header and with an OUI of 0x000000
02105          *  (encapsulated Ethernet) and a protocol
02106          *  ID of ETHERTYPE_IPX in the SNAP header.
02107          *
02108          * First, do the checks on LINUX_SLL_P_802_2
02109          * frames; generate the check for either
02110          * Ethernet_802.2 or Ethernet_SNAP frames, and
02111          * then put a check for LINUX_SLL_P_802_2 frames
02112          * before it.
02113          */
02114         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_MACPL, 0, BPF_B, (bpf_int32)LLCSAP_IPX);
02115         b1 = gen_snap(0x000000, ETHERTYPE_IPX);
02116         gen_or(b0, b1);
02117         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, LINUX_SLL_P_802_2);
02118         gen_and(b0, b1);
02119 
02120         /*
02121          * Now check for 802.3 frames and OR that with
02122          * the previous test.
02123          */
02124         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, LINUX_SLL_P_802_3);
02125         gen_or(b0, b1);
02126 
02127         /*
02128          * Now add the check for Ethernet_II frames, and
02129          * do that before checking for the other frame
02130          * types.
02131          */
02132         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H,
02133             (bpf_int32)ETHERTYPE_IPX);
02134         gen_or(b0, b1);
02135         return b1;
02136 
02137     case ETHERTYPE_ATALK:
02138     case ETHERTYPE_AARP:
02139         /*
02140          * EtherTalk (AppleTalk protocols on Ethernet link
02141          * layer) may use 802.2 encapsulation.
02142          */
02143 
02144         /*
02145          * Check for 802.2 encapsulation (EtherTalk phase 2?);
02146          * we check for the 802.2 protocol type in the
02147          * "Ethernet type" field.
02148          */
02149         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, LINUX_SLL_P_802_2);
02150 
02151         /*
02152          * 802.2-encapsulated ETHERTYPE_ATALK packets are
02153          * SNAP packets with an organization code of
02154          * 0x080007 (Apple, for Appletalk) and a protocol
02155          * type of ETHERTYPE_ATALK (Appletalk).
02156          *
02157          * 802.2-encapsulated ETHERTYPE_AARP packets are
02158          * SNAP packets with an organization code of
02159          * 0x000000 (encapsulated Ethernet) and a protocol
02160          * type of ETHERTYPE_AARP (Appletalk ARP).
02161          */
02162         if (proto == ETHERTYPE_ATALK)
02163             b1 = gen_snap(0x080007, ETHERTYPE_ATALK);
02164         else    /* proto == ETHERTYPE_AARP */
02165             b1 = gen_snap(0x000000, ETHERTYPE_AARP);
02166         gen_and(b0, b1);
02167 
02168         /*
02169          * Check for Ethernet encapsulation (Ethertalk
02170          * phase 1?); we just check for the Ethernet
02171          * protocol type.
02172          */
02173         b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H, (bpf_int32)proto);
02174 
02175         gen_or(b0, b1);
02176         return b1;
02177 
02178     default:
02179         if (proto <= ETHERMTU) {
02180             /*
02181              * This is an LLC SAP value, so the frames
02182              * that match would be 802.2 frames.
02183              * Check for the 802.2 protocol type
02184              * in the "Ethernet type" field, and
02185              * then check the DSAP.
02186              */
02187             b0 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H,
02188                 LINUX_SLL_P_802_2);
02189             b1 = gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_macpl, BPF_B,
02190                  (bpf_int32)proto);
02191             gen_and(b0, b1);
02192             return b1;
02193         } else {
02194             /*
02195              * This is an Ethernet type, so compare
02196              * the length/type field with it (if
02197              * the frame is an 802.2 frame, the length
02198              * field will be <= ETHERMTU, and, as
02199              * "proto" is > ETHERMTU, this test
02200              * will fail and the frame won't match,
02201              * which is what we want).
02202              */
02203             return gen_cmp(OR_LINK, off_linktype, BPF_H,
02204                 (bpf_int32)proto);
02205         }
02206     }
02207 }
02208 
02209 static struct slist *
02210 gen_load_prism_llprefixlen()
02211 {
02212     struct slist *s1, *s2;
02213     struct slist *sjeq_avs_cookie;
02214     struct slist *sjcommon;
02215 
02216     /*
02217      * This code is not compatible with the optimizer, as
02218      * we are generating jmp instructions within a normal
02219      * slist of instructions
02220      */
02221     no_optimize = 1;
02222 
02223     /*
02224      * Generate code to load the length of the radio header into
02225      * the register assigned to hold that length, if one has been
02226      * assigned.  (If one hasn't been assigned, no code we've
02227      * generated uses that prefix, so we don't need to generate any
02228      * code to load it.)
02229      *
02230      * Some Linux drivers use ARPHRD_IEEE80211_PRISM but sometimes
02231      * or always use the AVS header rather than the Prism header.
02232      * We load a 4-byte big-endian value at the beginning of the
02233      * raw packet data, and see whether, when masked with 0xFFFFF000,
02234      * it's equal to 0x80211000.  If so, that indicates that it's
02235      * an AVS header (the masked-out bits are the version number).
02236      * Otherwise, it's a Prism header.
02237      *
02238      * XXX - the Prism header is also, in theory, variable-length,
02239      * but no known software generates headers that aren't 144
02240      * bytes long.
02241      */
02242     if (reg_off_ll != -1) {
02243         /*
02244          * Load the cookie.
02245          */
02246         s1 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_W|BPF_ABS);
02247         s1->s.k = 0;
02248 
02249         /*
02250          * AND it with 0xFFFFF000.
02251          */
02252         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_AND|BPF_K);
02253         s2->s.k = 0xFFFFF000;
02254         sappend(s1, s2);
02255 
02256         /*
02257          * Compare with 0x80211000.
02258          */
02259         sjeq_avs_cookie = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JEQ));
02260         sjeq_avs_cookie->s.k = 0x80211000;
02261         sappend(s1, sjeq_avs_cookie);
02262 
02263         /*
02264          * If it's AVS:
02265          *
02266          * The 4 bytes at an offset of 4 from the beginning of
02267          * the AVS header are the length of the AVS header.
02268          * That field is big-endian.
02269          */
02270         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_W|BPF_ABS);
02271         s2->s.k = 4;
02272         sappend(s1, s2);
02273         sjeq_avs_cookie->s.jt = s2;
02274 
02275         /*
02276          * Now jump to the code to allocate a register
02277          * into which to save the header length and
02278          * store the length there.  (The "jump always"
02279          * instruction needs to have the k field set;
02280          * it's added to the PC, so, as we're jumping
02281          * over a single instruction, it should be 1.)
02282          */
02283         sjcommon = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JA));
02284         sjcommon->s.k = 1;
02285         sappend(s1, sjcommon);
02286 
02287         /*
02288          * Now for the code that handles the Prism header.
02289          * Just load the length of the Prism header (144)
02290          * into the A register.  Have the test for an AVS
02291          * header branch here if we don't have an AVS header.
02292          */
02293         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_W|BPF_IMM);
02294         s2->s.k = 144;
02295         sappend(s1, s2);
02296         sjeq_avs_cookie->s.jf = s2;
02297 
02298         /*
02299          * Now allocate a register to hold that value and store
02300          * it.  The code for the AVS header will jump here after
02301          * loading the length of the AVS header.
02302          */
02303         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02304         s2->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02305         sappend(s1, s2);
02306         sjcommon->s.jf = s2;
02307 
02308         /*
02309          * Now move it into the X register.
02310          */
02311         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX);
02312         sappend(s1, s2);
02313 
02314         return (s1);
02315     } else
02316         return (NULL);
02317 }
02318 
02319 static struct slist *
02320 gen_load_avs_llprefixlen()
02321 {
02322     struct slist *s1, *s2;
02323 
02324     /*
02325      * Generate code to load the length of the AVS header into
02326      * the register assigned to hold that length, if one has been
02327      * assigned.  (If one hasn't been assigned, no code we've
02328      * generated uses that prefix, so we don't need to generate any
02329      * code to load it.)
02330      */
02331     if (reg_off_ll != -1) {
02332         /*
02333          * The 4 bytes at an offset of 4 from the beginning of
02334          * the AVS header are the length of the AVS header.
02335          * That field is big-endian.
02336          */
02337         s1 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_W|BPF_ABS);
02338         s1->s.k = 4;
02339 
02340         /*
02341          * Now allocate a register to hold that value and store
02342          * it.
02343          */
02344         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02345         s2->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02346         sappend(s1, s2);
02347 
02348         /*
02349          * Now move it into the X register.
02350          */
02351         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX);
02352         sappend(s1, s2);
02353 
02354         return (s1);
02355     } else
02356         return (NULL);
02357 }
02358 
02359 static struct slist *
02360 gen_load_radiotap_llprefixlen()
02361 {
02362     struct slist *s1, *s2;
02363 
02364     /*
02365      * Generate code to load the length of the radiotap header into
02366      * the register assigned to hold that length, if one has been
02367      * assigned.  (If one hasn't been assigned, no code we've
02368      * generated uses that prefix, so we don't need to generate any
02369      * code to load it.)
02370      */
02371     if (reg_off_ll != -1) {
02372         /*
02373          * The 2 bytes at offsets of 2 and 3 from the beginning
02374          * of the radiotap header are the length of the radiotap
02375          * header; unfortunately, it's little-endian, so we have
02376          * to load it a byte at a time and construct the value.
02377          */
02378 
02379         /*
02380          * Load the high-order byte, at an offset of 3, shift it
02381          * left a byte, and put the result in the X register.
02382          */
02383         s1 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_B|BPF_ABS);
02384         s1->s.k = 3;
02385         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_LSH|BPF_K);
02386         sappend(s1, s2);
02387         s2->s.k = 8;
02388         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX);
02389         sappend(s1, s2);
02390 
02391         /*
02392          * Load the next byte, at an offset of 2, and OR the
02393          * value from the X register into it.
02394          */
02395         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_B|BPF_ABS);
02396         sappend(s1, s2);
02397         s2->s.k = 2;
02398         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_OR|BPF_X);
02399         sappend(s1, s2);
02400 
02401         /*
02402          * Now allocate a register to hold that value and store
02403          * it.
02404          */
02405         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02406         s2->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02407         sappend(s1, s2);
02408 
02409         /*
02410          * Now move it into the X register.
02411          */
02412         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX);
02413         sappend(s1, s2);
02414 
02415         return (s1);
02416     } else
02417         return (NULL);
02418 }
02419 
02420 /* 
02421  * At the moment we treat PPI as normal Radiotap encoded
02422  * packets. The difference is in the function that generates
02423  * the code at the beginning to compute the header length.
02424  * Since this code generator of PPI supports bare 802.11
02425  * encapsulation only (i.e. the encapsulated DLT should be
02426  * DLT_IEEE802_11) we generate code to check for this too;
02427  * that's done in finish_parse().
02428  */
02429 static struct slist *
02430 gen_load_ppi_llprefixlen()
02431 {
02432     struct slist *s1, *s2;
02433     
02434     /*
02435      * Generate code to load the length of the radiotap header
02436      * into the register assigned to hold that length, if one has
02437      * been assigned.
02438      */
02439     if (reg_off_ll != -1) {
02440         /*
02441          * The 2 bytes at offsets of 2 and 3 from the beginning
02442          * of the radiotap header are the length of the radiotap
02443          * header; unfortunately, it's little-endian, so we have
02444          * to load it a byte at a time and construct the value.
02445          */
02446 
02447         /*
02448          * Load the high-order byte, at an offset of 3, shift it
02449          * left a byte, and put the result in the X register.
02450          */
02451         s1 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_B|BPF_ABS);
02452         s1->s.k = 3;
02453         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_LSH|BPF_K);
02454         sappend(s1, s2);
02455         s2->s.k = 8;
02456         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX);
02457         sappend(s1, s2);
02458 
02459         /*
02460          * Load the next byte, at an offset of 2, and OR the
02461          * value from the X register into it.
02462          */
02463         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_B|BPF_ABS);
02464         sappend(s1, s2);
02465         s2->s.k = 2;
02466         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_OR|BPF_X);
02467         sappend(s1, s2);
02468 
02469         /*
02470          * Now allocate a register to hold that value and store
02471          * it.
02472          */
02473         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02474         s2->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02475         sappend(s1, s2);
02476 
02477         /*
02478          * Now move it into the X register.
02479          */
02480         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TAX);
02481         sappend(s1, s2);
02482 
02483         return (s1);
02484     } else
02485         return (NULL);
02486 }
02487 
02488 /*
02489  * Load a value relative to the beginning of the link-layer header after the 802.11
02490  * header, i.e. LLC_SNAP.
02491  * The link-layer header doesn't necessarily begin at the beginning
02492  * of the packet data; there might be a variable-length prefix containing
02493  * radio information.
02494  */
02495 static struct slist *
02496 gen_load_802_11_header_len(struct slist *s, struct slist *snext)
02497 {
02498     struct slist *s2;
02499     struct slist *sjset_data_frame_1;
02500     struct slist *sjset_data_frame_2;
02501     struct slist *sjset_qos;
02502     struct slist *sjset_radiotap_flags;
02503     struct slist *sjset_radiotap_tsft;
02504     struct slist *sjset_tsft_datapad, *sjset_notsft_datapad;
02505     struct slist *s_roundup;
02506 
02507     if (reg_off_macpl == -1) {
02508         /*
02509          * No register has been assigned to the offset of
02510          * the MAC-layer payload, which means nobody needs
02511          * it; don't bother computing it - just return
02512          * what we already have.
02513          */
02514         return (s);
02515     }
02516 
02517     /*
02518      * This code is not compatible with the optimizer, as
02519      * we are generating jmp instructions within a normal
02520      * slist of instructions
02521      */
02522     no_optimize = 1;
02523     
02524     /*
02525      * If "s" is non-null, it has code to arrange that the X register
02526      * contains the length of the prefix preceding the link-layer
02527      * header.
02528      *
02529      * Otherwise, the length of the prefix preceding the link-layer
02530      * header is "off_ll".
02531      */
02532     if (s == NULL) {
02533         /*
02534          * There is no variable-length header preceding the
02535          * link-layer header.
02536          *
02537          * Load the length of the fixed-length prefix preceding
02538          * the link-layer header (if any) into the X register,
02539          * and store it in the reg_off_macpl register.
02540          * That length is off_ll.
02541          */
02542         s = new_stmt(BPF_LDX|BPF_IMM);
02543         s->s.k = off_ll;
02544     }
02545 
02546     /*
02547      * The X register contains the offset of the beginning of the
02548      * link-layer header; add 24, which is the minimum length
02549      * of the MAC header for a data frame, to that, and store it
02550      * in reg_off_macpl, and then load the Frame Control field,
02551      * which is at the offset in the X register, with an indexed load.
02552      */
02553     s2 = new_stmt(BPF_MISC|BPF_TXA);
02554     sappend(s, s2);
02555     s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_ADD|BPF_K);
02556     s2->s.k = 24;
02557     sappend(s, s2);
02558     s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02559     s2->s.k = reg_off_macpl;
02560     sappend(s, s2);
02561 
02562     s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_IND|BPF_B);
02563     s2->s.k = 0;
02564     sappend(s, s2);
02565 
02566     /*
02567      * Check the Frame Control field to see if this is a data frame;
02568      * a data frame has the 0x08 bit (b3) in that field set and the
02569      * 0x04 bit (b2) clear.
02570      */
02571     sjset_data_frame_1 = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02572     sjset_data_frame_1->s.k = 0x08;
02573     sappend(s, sjset_data_frame_1);
02574         
02575     /*
02576      * If b3 is set, test b2, otherwise go to the first statement of
02577      * the rest of the program.
02578      */
02579     sjset_data_frame_1->s.jt = sjset_data_frame_2 = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02580     sjset_data_frame_2->s.k = 0x04;
02581     sappend(s, sjset_data_frame_2);
02582     sjset_data_frame_1->s.jf = snext;
02583 
02584     /*
02585      * If b2 is not set, this is a data frame; test the QoS bit.
02586      * Otherwise, go to the first statement of the rest of the
02587      * program.
02588      */
02589     sjset_data_frame_2->s.jt = snext;
02590     sjset_data_frame_2->s.jf = sjset_qos = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02591     sjset_qos->s.k = 0x80;  /* QoS bit */
02592     sappend(s, sjset_qos);
02593         
02594     /*
02595      * If it's set, add 2 to reg_off_macpl, to skip the QoS
02596      * field.
02597      * Otherwise, go to the first statement of the rest of the
02598      * program.
02599      */
02600     sjset_qos->s.jt = s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_MEM);
02601     s2->s.k = reg_off_macpl;
02602     sappend(s, s2);
02603     s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_ADD|BPF_IMM);
02604     s2->s.k = 2;
02605     sappend(s, s2);
02606     s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02607     s2->s.k = reg_off_macpl;
02608     sappend(s, s2);
02609 
02610     /*
02611      * If we have a radiotap header, look at it to see whether
02612      * there's Atheros padding between the MAC-layer header
02613      * and the payload.
02614      *
02615      * Note: all of the fields in the radiotap header are
02616      * little-endian, so we byte-swap all of the values
02617      * we test against, as they will be loaded as big-endian
02618      * values.
02619      */
02620     if (linktype == DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO) {
02621         /*
02622          * Is the IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_FLAGS bit (0x0000002) set
02623          * in the presence flag?
02624          */
02625         sjset_qos->s.jf = s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_ABS|BPF_W);
02626         s2->s.k = 4;
02627         sappend(s, s2);
02628 
02629         sjset_radiotap_flags = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02630         sjset_radiotap_flags->s.k = SWAPLONG(0x00000002);
02631         sappend(s, sjset_radiotap_flags);
02632 
02633         /*
02634          * If not, skip all of this.
02635          */
02636         sjset_radiotap_flags->s.jf = snext;
02637 
02638         /*
02639          * Otherwise, is the IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_TSFT bit set?
02640          */
02641         sjset_radiotap_tsft = sjset_radiotap_flags->s.jt =
02642             new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02643         sjset_radiotap_tsft->s.k = SWAPLONG(0x00000001);
02644         sappend(s, sjset_radiotap_tsft);
02645 
02646         /*
02647          * If IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_TSFT is set, the flags field is
02648          * at an offset of 16 from the beginning of the raw packet
02649          * data (8 bytes for the radiotap header and 8 bytes for
02650          * the TSFT field).
02651          *
02652          * Test whether the IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_F_DATAPAD bit (0x20)
02653          * is set.
02654          */
02655         sjset_radiotap_tsft->s.jt = s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_ABS|BPF_B);
02656         s2->s.k = 16;
02657         sappend(s, s2);
02658 
02659         sjset_tsft_datapad = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02660         sjset_tsft_datapad->s.k = 0x20;
02661         sappend(s, sjset_tsft_datapad);
02662 
02663         /*
02664          * If IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_TSFT is not set, the flags field is
02665          * at an offset of 8 from the beginning of the raw packet
02666          * data (8 bytes for the radiotap header).
02667          *
02668          * Test whether the IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_F_DATAPAD bit (0x20)
02669          * is set.
02670          */
02671         sjset_radiotap_tsft->s.jf = s2 = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_ABS|BPF_B);
02672         s2->s.k = 8;
02673         sappend(s, s2);
02674 
02675         sjset_notsft_datapad = new_stmt(JMP(BPF_JSET));
02676         sjset_notsft_datapad->s.k = 0x20;
02677         sappend(s, sjset_notsft_datapad);
02678 
02679         /*
02680          * In either case, if IEEE80211_RADIOTAP_F_DATAPAD is
02681          * set, round the length of the 802.11 header to
02682          * a multiple of 4.  Do that by adding 3 and then
02683          * dividing by and multiplying by 4, which we do by
02684          * ANDing with ~3.
02685          */
02686         s_roundup = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_MEM);
02687         s_roundup->s.k = reg_off_macpl;
02688         sappend(s, s_roundup);
02689         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_ADD|BPF_IMM);
02690         s2->s.k = 3;
02691         sappend(s, s2);
02692         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ALU|BPF_AND|BPF_IMM);
02693         s2->s.k = ~3;
02694         sappend(s, s2);
02695         s2 = new_stmt(BPF_ST);
02696         s2->s.k = reg_off_macpl;
02697         sappend(s, s2);
02698 
02699         sjset_tsft_datapad->s.jt = s_roundup;
02700         sjset_tsft_datapad->s.jf = snext;
02701         sjset_notsft_datapad->s.jt = s_roundup;
02702         sjset_notsft_datapad->s.jf = snext;
02703     } else
02704         sjset_qos->s.jf = snext;
02705 
02706     return s;
02707 }
02708 
02709 static void
02710 insert_compute_vloffsets(b)
02711     struct block *b;
02712 {
02713     struct slist *s;
02714 
02715     /*
02716      * For link-layer types that have a variable-length header
02717      * preceding the link-layer header, generate code to load
02718      * the offset of the link-layer header into the register
02719      * assigned to that offset, if any.
02720      */
02721     switch (linktype) {
02722 
02723     case DLT_PRISM_HEADER:
02724         s = gen_load_prism_llprefixlen();
02725         break;
02726 
02727     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO_AVS:
02728         s = gen_load_avs_llprefixlen();
02729         break;
02730 
02731     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO:
02732         s = gen_load_radiotap_llprefixlen();
02733         break;
02734 
02735     case DLT_PPI:
02736         s = gen_load_ppi_llprefixlen();
02737         break;
02738 
02739     default:
02740         s = NULL;
02741         break;
02742     }
02743 
02744     /*
02745      * For link-layer types that have a variable-length link-layer
02746      * header, generate code to load the offset of the MAC-layer
02747      * payload into the register assigned to that offset, if any.
02748      */
02749     switch (linktype) {
02750 
02751     case DLT_IEEE802_11:
02752     case DLT_PRISM_HEADER:
02753     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO_AVS:
02754     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO:
02755     case DLT_PPI:
02756         s = gen_load_802_11_header_len(s, b->stmts);
02757         break;
02758     }
02759 
02760     /*
02761      * If we have any offset-loading code, append all the
02762      * existing statements in the block to those statements,
02763      * and make the resulting list the list of statements
02764      * for the block.
02765      */
02766     if (s != NULL) {
02767         sappend(s, b->stmts);
02768         b->stmts = s;
02769     }
02770 }
02771 
02772 static struct block *
02773 gen_ppi_dlt_check(void)
02774 {
02775     struct slist *s_load_dlt;
02776     struct block *b;
02777 
02778     if (linktype == DLT_PPI)
02779     {
02780         /* Create the statements that check for the DLT
02781          */
02782         s_load_dlt = new_stmt(BPF_LD|BPF_W|BPF_ABS);
02783         s_load_dlt->s.k = 4;
02784 
02785         b = new_block(JMP(BPF_JEQ));
02786 
02787         b->stmts = s_load_dlt;
02788         b->s.k = SWAPLONG(DLT_IEEE802_11);
02789     }
02790     else
02791     {
02792         b = NULL;
02793     }
02794 
02795     return b;
02796 }
02797 
02798 static struct slist *
02799 gen_prism_llprefixlen(void)
02800 {
02801     struct slist *s;
02802 
02803     if (reg_off_ll == -1) {
02804         /*
02805          * We haven't yet assigned a register for the length
02806          * of the radio header; allocate one.
02807          */
02808         reg_off_ll = alloc_reg();
02809     }
02810 
02811     /*
02812      * Load the register containing the radio length
02813      * into the X register.
02814      */
02815     s = new_stmt(BPF_LDX|BPF_MEM);
02816     s->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02817     return s;
02818 }
02819 
02820 static struct slist *
02821 gen_avs_llprefixlen(void)
02822 {
02823     struct slist *s;
02824 
02825     if (reg_off_ll == -1) {
02826         /*
02827          * We haven't yet assigned a register for the length
02828          * of the AVS header; allocate one.
02829          */
02830         reg_off_ll = alloc_reg();
02831     }
02832 
02833     /*
02834      * Load the register containing the AVS length
02835      * into the X register.
02836      */
02837     s = new_stmt(BPF_LDX|BPF_MEM);
02838     s->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02839     return s;
02840 }
02841 
02842 static struct slist *
02843 gen_radiotap_llprefixlen(void)
02844 {
02845     struct slist *s;
02846 
02847     if (reg_off_ll == -1) {
02848         /*
02849          * We haven't yet assigned a register for the length
02850          * of the radiotap header; allocate one.
02851          */
02852         reg_off_ll = alloc_reg();
02853     }
02854 
02855     /*
02856      * Load the register containing the radiotap length
02857      * into the X register.
02858      */
02859     s = new_stmt(BPF_LDX|BPF_MEM);
02860     s->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02861     return s;
02862 }
02863 
02864 /* 
02865  * At the moment we treat PPI as normal Radiotap encoded
02866  * packets. The difference is in the function that generates
02867  * the code at the beginning to compute the header length.
02868  * Since this code generator of PPI supports bare 802.11
02869  * encapsulation only (i.e. the encapsulated DLT should be
02870  * DLT_IEEE802_11) we generate code to check for this too.
02871  */
02872 static struct slist *
02873 gen_ppi_llprefixlen(void)
02874 {
02875     struct slist *s;
02876 
02877     if (reg_off_ll == -1) {
02878         /*
02879          * We haven't yet assigned a register for the length
02880          * of the radiotap header; allocate one.
02881          */
02882         reg_off_ll = alloc_reg();
02883     }
02884 
02885     /*
02886      * Load the register containing the PPI length
02887      * into the X register.
02888      */
02889     s = new_stmt(BPF_LDX|BPF_MEM);
02890     s->s.k = reg_off_ll;
02891     return s;
02892 }
02893 
02894 /*
02895  * Generate code to compute the link-layer header length, if necessary,
02896  * putting it into the X register, and to return either a pointer to a
02897  * "struct slist" for the list of statements in that code, or NULL if
02898  * no code is necessary.
02899  */
02900 static struct slist *
02901 gen_llprefixlen(void)
02902 {
02903     switch (linktype) {
02904 
02905     case DLT_PRISM_HEADER:
02906         return gen_prism_llprefixlen();
02907 
02908     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO_AVS:
02909         return gen_avs_llprefixlen();
02910 
02911     case DLT_IEEE802_11_RADIO:
02912         return gen_radiotap_llprefixlen();
02913 
02914     case DLT_PPI:
02915         return gen_ppi_llprefixlen();
02916 
02917     default:
02918         return NULL;
02919     }
02920 }
02921 
02922 /*
02923  * Generate code to load the register containing the offset of the
02924  * MAC-layer payload into the X register; if no register for that offset
02925  * has been allocated, allocate it first.
